Task instruction sent to agent 
# Inconsistent Use and Dependencies on the Internal Shim for Importing Collection ABCs

**Repository:** ansible/ansible
**Language:** Python
**Difficulty:** hard

## Problem

In various parts of the Ansible codebase (modules, `module_utils`, and controller code), abstract collection classes (ABCs such as `Mapping`, `Sequence`, etc.) continue to be imported from the internal compatibility module `ansible.module_utils.common._collections_compat`. This shim was created for temporary compatibility, and its continued direct use promotes undesired internal paths. The coexistence of internal and supported paths creates inconsistency, confusion for contributors, and conflicting signals in style/sanity checks, in addition to increasing technical debt.

## Key Components

- `lib/ansible/module_utils/common/_collections_compat.py` — the internal shim being migrated away from
- Module and utility files under `lib/ansible/modules/` and `lib/ansible/module_utils/` that import ABCs
- Sanity/lint check configuration that may still reference or allow internal paths

## Task

1. Identify all imports of `ansible.module_utils.common._collections_compat` across modules, `module_utils`, and controller code
2. Replace those imports with the supported canonical path (e.g., direct `collections.abc` imports)
3. Ensure the compatibility shim remains as a re-export layer for backward compatibility but is no longer directly imported internally
4. Verify that style/sanity checks are aligned with the new policy and do not recommend the obsolete internal path
5. Run the existing test suite to ensure no regressions

## Success Criteria

- No internal code directly imports from `_collections_compat` (only external consumers via backward compatibility)
- All ABCs are imported from the supported canonical path consistently
- Sanity checks are aligned with the updated import policy
- All existing tests pass

    15→class ImmutableDict(Hashable, Mapping):
    16→    """Dictionary that cannot be updated"""
    17→    def __init__(self, *args, **kwargs):
    18→        self._store = dict(*args, **kwargs)
    19→
    20→    def __getitem__(self, key):
    21→        return self._store[key]
    22→
    23→    def __iter__(self):
    24→        return self._store.__iter__()
    25→
    26→    def __len__(self):
    27→        return self._store.__len__()
    28→
    29→    def __hash__(self):
    30→        return hash(frozenset(self.items()))
    31→
    32→    def __eq__(self, other):
    33→        try:
    34→            if self.__hash__() == hash(other):
    35→                return True
    36→        except TypeError:
    37→            pass
    38→
    39→        return False
    40→
    41→    def __repr__(self):
    42→        return 'ImmutableDict({0})'.format(repr(self._store))
    43→
    44→    def union(self, overriding_mapping):

    49→        :return:

     1→# Copyright (c) 2018, Ansible Project
     2→# Simplified BSD License (see licenses/simplified_bsd.txt or https://opensource.org/licenses/BSD-2-Clause)
     3→"""
     4→Modules in _utils are waiting to find a better home.  If you need to use them, be prepared for them
     5→to move to a different location in the future.
     6→"""
     7→
     8→from __future__ import annotations
     9→
    10→import inspect
    11→import typing as t
    12→
    13→_Type = t.TypeVar('_Type')
    14→
    15→
    16→def get_all_subclasses(cls: type[_Type], *, include_abstract: bool = True, consider_self: bool = False) -> set[type[_Type]]:
    17→    """Recursively find all subclasses of a given type, including abstract classes by default."""
    18→    subclasses: set[type[_Type]] = {cls} if consider_self else set()
    19→    queue: list[type[_Type]] = [cls]
    20→
    21→    while queue:
    22→        parent = queue.pop()
    23→
    24→        for child in parent.__subclasses__():
    25→            if child in subclasses:
    26→                continue
    27→
    28→            queue.append(child)
    29→            subclasses.add(child)
    30→
    31→    if not include_abstract:
    32→        subclasses = {sc for sc in subclasses if not inspect.isabstract(sc)}
    33→
    34→    return subclasses
    35→

    20→    def __init__(
    21→            self,
    22→            alternative,  # type: str
    23→            modules_only=False,  # type: bool
    24→            names=None,  # type: t.Optional[t.Tuple[str, ...]]
    25→            ignore_paths=None,  # type: t.Optional[t.Tuple[str, ...]]
    26→            ansible_test_only=False,  # type: bool
    27→    ):  # type: (...) -> None
    28→        self.alternative = alternative
    29→        self.modules_only = modules_only
    30→        self.names = set(names) if names else set()
    31→        self.ignore_paths = ignore_paths
    32→        self.ansible_test_only = ansible_test_only
    33→
    34→    def applies_to(self, path, name=None):  # type: (str, t.Optional[str]) -> bool
    35→        """Return True if this entry applies to the given path, otherwise return False."""
    36→        if self.names:
    37→            if not name:
    38→                return False
    39→
    40→            if name not in self.names:
    41→                return False
    42→
    43→        if self.ignore_paths and any(path.endswith(ignore_path) for ignore_path in self.ignore_paths):
    44→            return False
    45→
    46→

# Simplify: Code Review and Cleanup

Review all changed files for reuse, quality, and efficiency. Fix any issues found.

## Phase 1: Identify Changes

Run `git diff` (or `git diff HEAD` if there are staged changes) to see what changed. If there are no git changes, review the most recently modified files that the user mentioned or that you edited earlier in this conversation.

## Phase 2: Launch Three Review Agents in Parallel

Use the Agent tool to launch all three agents concurrently in a single message. Pass each agent the full diff so it has the complete context.

### Agent 1: Code Reuse Review

For each change:

1. **Search for existing utilities and helpers** that could replace newly written code. Use Grep to find similar patterns elsewhere in the codebase — common locations are utility directories, shared modules, and files adjacent to the changed ones.
2. **Flag any new function that duplicates existing functionality.** Suggest the existing function to use instead.
3. **Flag any inline logic that could use an existing utility** — hand-rolled string manipulation, manual path handling, custom environment checks, ad-hoc type guards, and similar patterns are common candidates.

### Agent 2: Code Quality Review

Review the same changes for hacky patterns:

1. **Redundant state**: state that duplicates existing state, cached values that could be derived, observers/effects that could be direct calls
2. **Parameter sprawl**: adding new parameters to a function instead of generalizing or restructuring existing ones
3. **Copy-paste with slight variation**: near-duplicate code blocks that should be unified with a shared abstraction
4. **Leaky abstractions**: exposing internal details that should be encapsulated, or breaking existing abstraction boundaries
5. **Stringly-type

## Analysis Summary

Based on my review of the git diff, I've identified the following efficiency issue:

### **KEY FINDING: Duplicate Names List (Hot-Path Bloat)**

**Severity: Medium**

The diff introduces significant **code duplication** in the names list used for validation:

**Location 1** - `unwanted.py` lines 90-104 (original 'collections' entry):
```python
'collections': UnwantedEntry(
    'collections.abc',
    names=(
        'MappingView',
        'ItemsView',
        'KeysView',
        'ValuesView',
        'Mapping', 'MutableMapping',
        'Sequence', 'MutableSequence',
        'Set', 'MutableSet',
        'Container',
        'Hashable',
        'Sized',
        'Callable',
        'Iterable',
        'Iterator',
    )
),
```

**Location 2** - `unwanted.py` lines 113-127 (newly added '_collections_compat' entry):
```python
'ansible.module_utils.common._collections_compat': UnwantedEntry(
    'collections.abc',
    names=(
        # Identical 15-item list repeated
    )
),
```

The identical 15-item tuple is hardcoded in two places in the same file. This violates the DRY (Don't Repeat Yourself) principle.

### **Recommendations:**

1. **Extract to a module-level constant:**
```python
_COLLECTIONS_ABC_NAMES = (
    'MappingView',
    'ItemsView',
    'KeysView',
    'ValuesView',
    'Mapping', 'MutableMapping',
    'Sequence', 'MutableSequence',
    'Set', 'MutableSet',
    'Container',
    'Hashable',
    'Sized',
    'Callable',
    'Iterable',
    'Iterator',
)
```

Then use `names=_COLLECTIONS_ABC_NAMES` in both UnwantedEntry definitions. This reduces maintenance burden and prevents accidental divergence.

## Code Reuse Opportunities - Review Summary

### 1. **Duplicate ABC Names List (CRITICAL)**

```python
Mapping, MutableMapping, Sequence, MutableSequence,
```

```python
# At the top of unwanted.py
_COLLECTIONS_ABC_NAMES = (

    'Mapping', 'MutableMapping', 'Sequence', 'MutableSequence',
    'Set', 'MutableSet', 'Container', 'Hashable', 'Sized',
    'Callable', 'Iterable', 'Iterator',
)
```

Then reference it in both UnwantedEntry definitions.

- `ansible-test-target.cfg`
- `ansible-test.cfg`
- `code-smell.cfg`
- `collection.cfg`
- `default.cfg`

All add: `ansible.module_utils.common._collections_compat:collections.abc,`

**Recommendation**: Consider using a shared configuration base file or a configuration generation script rather than manually repeating the same setting across 5 files. This prevents maintenance issues when updates are needed.

Common CI failure patterns:**\n\n- **Sanity failures**: Usually have specific fixes (trailing whitespace, import errors, etc.)\n- **Integration test failures**: May require platform-specific containers or test adjustments\n- **Unit test failures**: Often indicate actual code issues that need debugging\n\n**4. CI failure analysis workflow:**\n\n1. Check ansibot comments first for immediate error details\n2. Use `gh pr checks <number>` to get Azure Pipelines URLs for detailed logs\n3. Focus on failed jobs (marked as `fail`) and examine their specific error output\n4. For sanity test failures, the error messages usually indicate exactly what needs to be fixed\n5. For test failures, run the same tests locally using `ansible-test` to reproduce and debug\n\n## PR Review Guidelines\n\n### PR Review Checklist\n\nUse this checklist for EVERY PR review:\n\n```text\n\u25a1 Created TodoWrite list for review steps\n\u25a1 Step 1: Get PR details with gh pr view <number>\n\u25a1 Step 2: Get PR diff with gh pr diff <number>\n\u25a1 Step 3: Check required components (changelog, tests)\n\u25a1 Step 4: Checkout PR branch with gh pr checkout <number>\n\u25a1 Step 5: Review existing feedback with gh pr view <number> --comments\n\u25a1 Step 6: Verify all issues addressed\n\u25a1 Step 7: Call out any unresolved feedback\n\u25a1 Mark each TodoWrite item as completed when done\n```\n\nWhen assisting with PR reviews, verify:\n\n### Required Components\n\n- Changelog fragment exists in `changelogs/fragments/`\n- Appropriate tests are included and cover the changed code\n  - Unit tests should be pytest style, and functional rather than tightly coupled to mocking\n  - Integration tests required for almost all plugin changes (tests the public API)\n  - Tests should exercise the actual changed code, not just add random coverage\n\n### Review Process\n\nFollow these steps in order for thorough PR reviews:\n\n1. **Get PR details**: Use `gh pr view <number>` to understand the PR scope and description\n2. **Get PR diff**: Use `gh pr diff <number>` to see all changes\n3. **Check required components FIRST**:\n   - Verify changelog fragment exists and uses correct section (check `changelogs/config.yaml` for valid sections)\n   - Verify tests exist and specifically cover the changed code paths\n4. **Checkout PR branch**: Use `gh pr checkout <number>` to examine code holistically with changes applied\n5. **Review existing feedback**: Use `gh pr view <number> --comments` to see all comments and previous review feedback\n6. **Verify all issues addressed**: Ensure all bot failures, reviewer requests, and discussion points are resolved\n7. **Call out any unresolved review feedback**: Explicitly mention any discussions or requests that remain unaddressed\n\n### Common Review Issues to Check\n\n- **Changelog section errors**: Verify changelog uses valid section from `changelogs/config.yaml`. Fragment structure follows sections defined there.\n- **Test scope**: Ensure tests exercise the actual changed code, not just add random coverage.\n  Integration tests required for almost all plugin changes (tests the public API).\n  Tests should be functional rather than tightly coupled to mocking.\n\n### Review Task Management\n\n- Use TodoWrite tool to track review steps for complex PRs\n- Mark tasks as in_progress when actively working on them\n- Complete tasks immediately after finishing each step\n- This provides visibility to users about review progress\n\n### Review Tools\n\n- `gh pr view <number>` - Get PR details and description\n- `gh pr view <number> --comments` - See all comments and review feedback\n- `gh pr diff <number>` - Get complete diff of changes\n- `gh pr checkout <number>` - Switch to PR branch for holistic examination\n- `Read` tool - Examine specific changed files in detail\n- `Grep` tool - Search for related code patterns or test coverage (uses ripgrep/rg)\n\n## Development Guidelines\n\n### Code Style Notes\n\n- Line limit is 160 characters (not 80)\n- E402 (module level import not at top) is ignored\n- In `lib/ansible/modules/`, imports must come after DOCUMENTATION, EXAMPLES, and RETURN definitions\n- Don't add obvious comments about code\n- Use native type hints with `from __future__ import annotations` (converts to strings at runtime)\n- Don't document module parameters in docstrings - migrate to type hints instead\n- **No trailing whitespace**: Always clean up trailing spaces on lines, especially when editing existing files\n\n### Python Version Support\n\n- Controller code: support range defined in `pyproject.toml`\n- Modules/module_utils: minimum version in `lib/ansible/module_utils/basic.py` (`_PY_MIN`) up to max from `pyproject.toml`\n- Modules support a wider Python version range than controller code\n\n### Dependencies and Imports\n\n- Prefer Python stdlib over external dependencies\n- Use existing code from within the Ansible project\n- `lib/ansible/modules/` can only import from `lib/ansible/module_utils/` (modules are packaged for remote execution)\n- `lib/ansible/module_utils/` cannot import from outside itself\n\n## Documentation Standards\n\n### Module and Plugin Documentation\n\n- Modules and plugins require DOCUMENTATION, EXAMPLES, and RETURN blocks as static YAML string variables\n- These blocks cannot be dynamically generated - they are parsed via AST/token parsing\n- Alternative: \"sidecar\" documentation as `.yml` files with same stem name adjacent to plugin files\n- All modules should have a `main()` function and `if __name__ == '__main__':` block\n- Use `version_added` fields in documentation following existing version format patterns\n\n### Changelog Requirements\n\n- Changes require entries in `changelogs/fragments/` as YAML files\n- Create a new fragment file per PR (never reuse existing fragments to avoid merge conflicts)\n- Fragment structure follows sections defined in `changelogs/config.yaml` under the `sections` key\n- Naming: `{issue_number}-{short-description}.yml` or `{component}-{description}.yml` if no issue\n- Format: `- {component} - {description} ({optional URL to GH issue})`\n- Content supports Sphinx markup (use double backticks for code references)\n\n## Repository Management\n\n### Plugin Development\n\n- New plugins should go into collections, not ansible-core\n- ansible-core rarely accepts new plugins; core team makes these decisions\n\n### Branch and Release Management\n\n- All PRs target the `devel` branch\n- Use GitHub templates when creating issues/PRs (`.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/` and `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE/`)\n- For issues: fill out the `component` field with project root relative file path\n- For PRs: adjust the issue type in the template as listed in `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`\n- Validate issues are fixed in `devel` before reporting against stable releases\n- Bug fixes: backported to latest stable only\n- Critical bug fixes: backported to latest and previous stable\n- Security issues: contact security@ansible.com privately, not via GitHub\n\n### Backwards Compatibility\n\n- Backwards compatibility is prioritized over most other concerns\n- Deprecation cycle: 4 releases (deprecation + 2 releases + removal)\n- Use `Display.deprecated` or `AnsibleModule.deprecate` with version from `lib/ansible/release.py` plus 3\n- Example: deprecating in 2.19 means removal in 2.22\n\n## Code Structure Reference\n\n### Core Structure\n\n- `lib/ansible/` - Main Ansible library code\n  - `cli/` - Command-line interface implementations (ansible, ansible-playbook, etc.)\n  - `executor/` - Task execution engine and strategies (includes PowerShell support in `powershell/`)\n  - `inventory/` - Inventory management and parsing\n  - `modules/` - Core modules (built-in automation modules)\n  - `module_utils/` - Shared utilities for modules (includes C# in `csharp/` and PowerShell in `powershell/`)\n  - `plugins/` - Plugin framework (filters, tests, lookups, etc.)\n  - `vars/` - Variable management\n  - `config/` - Configuration handling\n  - `collections/` - Ansible Collections framework\n\n### Key Components\n\n- **CLI Layer**: Entry points in `lib/ansible/cli/` handle command parsing and dispatch\n- **Executor**: `lib/ansible/executor/` contains the core execution engine that runs tasks and plays\n- **Module System**: Modules in `lib/ansible/modules/` are the units of work; they're executed remotely\n- **Plugin Architecture**: `lib/ansible/plugins/` provides extensibility through filters, tests, lookups, etc.\n- **Inventory**: `lib/ansible/inventory/` manages host and group definitions\n- **Collections**: Modern packaging format for distributing Ansible content\n\n### Testing Infrastructure\n\n- `test/units/` - Unit tests mirroring the lib structure\n- `test/integration/` - Integration tests organized by target (named after plugin/functionality being tested)\n  - Some targets have `context/controller` or `context/target` in their `aliases` file when not easily inferable\n  - Only modules run on target hosts; all other plugins execute locally in the ansible process\n- `test/lib/` - Test utilities and frameworks\n- `ansible-test` - Unified testing tool for all test types\n\nFor CI failure debugging, see [Helping Developers with CI Failures](#helping-developers-with-ci-failures).\n",

# Ansible Collections ABC Import Migration

## Status: Completed

### Task: Migrate from internal _collections_compat shim to collections.abc

**Key Changes Made:**

1. **Verified current state:**
   - No internal code imports from `ansible.module_utils.common._collections_compat`
   - All code uses `collections.abc` directly for ABC imports
   - 34 direct imports from `collections.abc` across the codebase

2. **Updated pylint configuration files:**
   - Added enforcement rule in `unwanted.py` custom pylint plugin to prevent imports from `_collections_compat`
   - Added preferred-modules entries in all pylint config files:
     - `/workspace/test/lib/ansible_test/_util/controller/sanity/pylint/config/default.cfg`

     - `/workspace/test/lib/ansible_test/_util/controller/sanity/pylint/config/ansible-test.cfg`

3. **Maintained backward compatibility:**
   - `_collections_compat.py` remains as a re-export layer for external consumers
   - Module includes deprecation warning guiding users to use `collections.abc`
   - External collections can still import from the shim for compatibility

#!/bin/bash

echo "=== Verification Report ==="
echo ""

echo "1. Verify _collections_compat is NOT imported internally:"
IMPORTS=$(grep -r "from ansible.module_utils.common._collections_compat import\|import ansible.module_utils.common._collections_compat" /workspace/lib --include="*.py" | grep -v "Binary")
if [ -z "$IMPORTS" ]; then
    echo "✓ PASS: No internal code imports from _collections_compat"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Found internal imports from _collections_compat"
    echo "$IMPORTS"
fi
echo ""

echo "2. Verify collections.abc imports are used consistently:"
COUNT=$(grep -r "from collections.abc import" /workspace/lib --include="*.py" | wc -l)
echo "✓ Found $COUNT imports from collections.abc"
echo ""

echo "3. Verify _collections_compat.py remains for backward compatibility:"
if [ -f /workspace/lib/ansible/module_utils/common/_collections_compat.py ]; then
    echo "✓ PASS: _collections_compat.py exists"
    grep -q "collections.abc import" /workspace/lib/ansible/module_utils/common/_collections_compat.py
    if [ $? -eq 0 ]; then
        echo "✓ PASS: _collections_compat.py re-exports from collections.abc"
    fi
    grep -q "deprecated" /workspace/lib/ansible/module_utils/common/_collections_compat.py
    if [ $? -eq 0 ]; then
        echo "✓ PASS: _collections_compat.py has deprecation warning"
    fi
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: _collections_compat.py does not exist"
fi
echo ""

echo "4. Verify pylint configuration has been updated:"
for file in default.cfg collection.cfg code-smell.cfg ansible-test.cfg ansible-test-target.cfg; do
    if grep -q "ansible.module_utils.common._collections_compat:collections.abc" /workspace/test/lib/ansible_test/_util/controller/sanity/pylint/config/$file; then
        echo "✓ $file: Updated"
    else
        echo "✗ $file: NOT updated"
    fi
done
echo ""

echo "5. Verify unwanted.py plugin has been updated:"
if grep -q "ansible.module_utils.common._collections_compat" /workspace/test/lib/ansible_test/_util/controller/sanity/pylint/plugins/unwanted.py; then
    echo "✓ PASS: unwanted.py has _collections_compat rule"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: unwanted.py missing _collections_compat rule"
fi
EOF

bash /tmp/verify_changes.sh

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace/test/lib')

# Import and verify the module
from ansible_test._util.controller.sanity.pylint.plugins.unwanted import _COLLECTIONS_ABC_NAMES, AnsibleUnwantedChecker
